  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fe1f758b-611d-40c6-bea0-ad58291a7e6f'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8392458630192426728">D-Day is approaching. They don’t know where or when, but the Germans know it'll be soon, and for Felicity “Flick” Clairet, the stakes have never been higher. A senior agent in the ranks of the Special Operations Executive (SOE) responsible for sabotage, Flick has survived to become one of Britain’s most effective operatives in Northern France. She knows that the Germans’ a</span>
  <span id="freeText8392458630192426728" style="display:none">D-Day is approaching. They don’t know where or when, but the Germans know it'll be soon, and for Felicity “Flick” Clairet, the stakes have never been higher. A senior agent in the ranks of the Special Operations Executive (SOE) responsible for sabotage, Flick has survived to become one of Britain’s most effective operatives in Northern France. She knows that the Germans’ ability to thwart the Allied attack depends upon their lines of communications, and in the days before the invasion no target is of greater strategic importance than the largest telephone exchange in Europe.<br /><br />But when Flick and her Resistance-leader husband try a direct, head-on assault that goes horribly wrong, her world turns upside down. Her group destroyed, her husband missing, her superiors unsure of her, her own confidence badly shaken, she has one last chance at the target, but the challenge, once daunting, is now near impossible. The new plan requires an all-woman team, none of them professionals, to be assembled and trained within days. Code-named the Jackdaws, they will attempt to infiltrate the exchange under the noses of the Germans—but the Germans are waiting for them now and have plans of their own. There are secrets Flick does not know—secrets within the German ranks, secrets among her hastily recruited team, secrets among those she trusts the most. And as the hours tick down to the point of no return, most daunting of all, there are secrets within herself. . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="8392458630192426728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2621656211?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Ilie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Ilie" href="/user/show/21690081-dana-ilie">Dana Ilie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21690081-dana-ilie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2621656211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1875286514279580444">This is a heart-racing, brilliantly fast-paced and gripping read. To merely call it 'exciting' would be an understatement. The plot is fantastically well-written, bringing together drama, history and tangible emotion. This is certainly not a book which can be easily put down.<br/>Follett not only knows how to tell a fantastic story and captivate the reader, he also knows exactly what the reader wants. The ending is just as gripping as the rest of the book and I can guarantee you will not be disappoin</span>
  <span id="freeText1875286514279580444" style="display:none">This is a heart-racing, brilliantly fast-paced and gripping read. To merely call it 'exciting' would be an understatement. The plot is fantastically well-written, bringing together drama, history and tangible emotion. This is certainly not a book which can be easily put down.<br />Follett not only knows how to tell a fantastic story and captivate the reader, he also knows exactly what the reader wants. The ending is just as gripping as the rest of the book and I can guarantee you will not be disappointed by it.<br />The plot of "Jackdaws" is realistic; many women served in the war, and some of them paid the ultimate sacrifice. Details of how agents were trained, how they reached their destinations in France, and the types of attacks they carried out alongside the French Resistance are accurate. Through this we are able to see the fear and horror facing those who worked behind enemy lines, yet also their courage and resourcefulness, and in this respect I can highly recommend this novel.<br /><br />On the other hand, I did find some aspects of "Jackdaws" a little too far-fetched. It would have been possible to put together an all-female group, but no agents would have been sent out with the limited training that the characters in this novel received. Also, some of the characters were incredibly blasé about the dangers facing them, behaving almost as though they were on holiday rather than on a secret mission behind enemy lines. Having said that, this is historical fiction and so one can suspend belief a little in exchange for a good story. And ‘Jackdaws’ is that. The plotting is clear, the action almost constant, the suspense engaging.<br /><br />Alongside the story of Flick and her group we also have the story of Dieter Franck, a German Intelligence officer whose character is full of contradictions – willing to do whatever is necessary to achieve his aims, yet feeling the guilt at what those actions entail; a loving husband, yet a man who also loves his mistress; a man who upholds the German ideal yet has feelings for a Jew. With Franck, and the other main characters in this novel, Mr Follett explores human psychology showing us the complexity of human relationships and how our feelings for others can colour our actions.<br /><br />All in all, "Jackdaws" is a good war-time thriller. Anyone who enjoys a fast-paced story set during the Second World War will enjoy this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1875286514279580444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8225077847805489849">Reading <i>Jackdaws</i>, like other Ken Follett titles I've read, is kind of like riding a moped. It's a lot of fun, but all the same you really don't want to be seen enjoying it. For me reading Follett is one of those guilty pleasures, where you know it isn't the best writing out there, the characters aren't particularly well developed, and in general the book isn't ground breaking or noteworthy in any way -- and yet you keep reading, because secretly it's kind of fun.<br/>If you like WWII fiction with lot</span>
  <span id="freeText8225077847805489849" style="display:none">Reading <i>Jackdaws</i>, like other Ken Follett titles I've read, is kind of like riding a moped. It's a lot of fun, but all the same you really don't want to be seen enjoying it. For me reading Follett is one of those guilty pleasures, where you know it isn't the best writing out there, the characters aren't particularly well developed, and in general the book isn't ground breaking or noteworthy in any way -- and yet you keep reading, because secretly it's kind of fun.<br />If you like WWII fiction with lots of action and don't mind stereotypical characters, then Follett's your man.</span>

<div id="review_2402461307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2402461307" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41763158-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525599242p2/41763158.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2402461307?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/41763158-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330509909" href="/book/show/7328279-jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=insufferable-main-characters">insufferable-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=ww2">ww2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=cover-envy">cover-envy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=wannabe-feminist">wannabe-feminist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=i-don-t-want-you-to-come-on-my-face">i-don-t-want-you-to-come-on-my-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=dishonour-on-your-cow">dishonour-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=you-n-me-could-write-a-bad-romance">you-n-me-could-write-a-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41763158-jess?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2402461307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8812122409225462817"><b>I’m not even going to attempt to be diplomatic, so buckle yourselves in because this book made me angry.</b><br/><br/>I’m surprised this has such a decent rating. <i>Jackdaws</i> is a grim mockery of the dedication and fierce bravery of the SOE girls. It exploits a very real and turbulent episode in European history, failing to present the complexity of the sacrifice these women were willing to make - many gave their lives. What is marketed as an intense action-packed thriller is nothing more than a completely impla</span>
  <span id="freeText8812122409225462817" style="display:none"><b>I’m not even going to attempt to be diplomatic, so buckle yourselves in because this book made me angry.</b><br /><br />I’m surprised this has such a decent rating. <i>Jackdaws</i> is a grim mockery of the dedication and fierce bravery of the SOE girls. It exploits a very real and turbulent episode in European history, failing to present the complexity of the sacrifice these women were willing to make - many gave their lives. What is marketed as an intense action-packed thriller is nothing more than a completely implausible troupe of women squabbling, bitching about each other, instigating cat fights and hooking up with every volunteer in a fifty mile radius. <br /><br />Follett’s presentation of women is <i>sickening</i>. The Jackdaws are never established as real characters beyond constant reminders of their sex appeal. Follett has a needless preoccupation with the objectification of women which seems to serve no other purpose than as an attempt to villainise the antagonist or else add some sort of racy element that the unnecessary sex scenes fail to provide (they read like bad smutty fanfic). It’s also obvious that Follett was attempting some shade of free indirect style by sporadically adopting different characters’ voices, but the female perspectives are especially cringey. Follett endows the Jackdaws with stereotypically ‘girly’ lines in an attempt to emulate the female mindset. Hackneyed examples include: <i> “I’m sorry for being such a girl”</i> and the classic, <i> “My bum is too big!”.</i> Look, as a real life (cisgender) female, I can testify that the size of my arse would be the <i>last</i> thing on my mind if I were facing the prospect of imminent capture and torture. <br /><br />I guess <i>Jackdaws</i> is supposed to be some groundbreaking feminist masterpiece simply because it puts women center stage amid the androcentricity of war - but to me, the Jackdaws are hardly the epitome of ‘strong female characters’. Flick is nothing but a fighting machine with breasts, (<i> “a tiny bundle of sex appeal”</i> and yes, that is an actual line) something which apparently makes her an undisputed feminist. Although other characters frequently supply helpful asides about how brave, intelligent, [insert other stereotype here] she is, Flick never does <i>anything</i> to justify these claims. Don't get me wrong, I'm all for female empowerment, but I thoroughly disagree with how Follett went about it. <i>Jackdaws</i> heavily insinuates that for a woman to be on an equal footing with men, she must be endowed with masculine qualities to make her like a man, and/or the men around her need to be degraded to incompetent idiots. To me, this completely contradicts the concept of gender equality and it's not fair - on men or women. Strong in the sense of physicality or capability is only one side of the coin; a character needs some level of vulnerability and empathy otherwise they will never have the need to be brave, or indeed strong. Being able to fire a gun alone does not make you brave or admirable. Besides, a primitive lust for violence is not a particularly appealing trait in <i>anyone</i>. <br /><br />Every character was achingly stale and prone to stereotype. Flick was a ripoff of Nancy Wake, the openly bawdy SOE agent, complete with a French lover and a codename that I assume was supposed to be lyrical like ‘The White Mouse’... but ‘Leopardess’ was just so obviously sultry that it had me snorting my disapproval. Other characters were defined entirely by their sexuality. It’s honourable that the effort was made to represent LGBTQ+, but these moments are so sporadic and contrived it feels to me as though Follett was trying <i>too</i> hard to be inclusive without actually doing the LGBTQ+ characters justice. These characters have no other values or traits other than their sexuality which does a disservice to both the characters themselves as well as the author. Is there a need to simply label a character as LGBTQ, tick a box, and have them play no other function in the story? People are <i>more</i> than just their sexuality. Ultimately, none of the characters were particularly <i>likeable</i>... besides from the antagonist and his sidekick. You know there’s a problem when you find yourself rooting unconditionally for the killer.<br /><br /><i>Jackdaws</i> reads like a bad action movie. The writing is, quite honestly, appalling; it’s ameteur and brimming with clunky phrases. My favourite lines included: “<i>Your security stinks.</i>” and <i>'The torture chamber gave him the creeps.'</i> The juvenile prose is incongruous with the tidbits of historical exposition which feel like transcribed verbatim excerpts from documentaries. This is in many ways a research-heavy piece, and certain scenes were obviously orchestrated with no other purpose than as an opportunity for Follett to show off how much research he’d done rather than offering any helpful insight into the story or moving the plot forward. <i>Jackdaws</i> is also full of specious and convenient plot twists; Follett is excessively melodramatic and uses numerous close calls in an attempt to build tension and suspense - but it only belies the gravity of the situation. Inevitably, this all builds up to a saccharine happy ending. Something that should've been emotionally compelling, wasn’t. <br /><br /><i>Jackdaws</i> is junk reading. If you like badly written Harlequin Romances masquerading as gritty espionage, give it a go. This was, quite simply, the thriller that failed to thrill.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8812122409225462817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166786005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4455636038119076059">"Exactly fifty women were sent into France as secret agents by the Special Operations Executive during the Second World War. Of those, thirty-six survived the war. The other fourteen gave their lives. This book is dedicated to all of them."<br/><br/>So. Damn. Good. <br/><br/>Ken Follett is best known for his sweeping epics Pillars of the Earth, World Without End, and Fall of Giants which span decades, but in Jackdaws he manages to apply his same talent for engrossing description into a story that takes 10 days. The</span>
  <span id="freeText4455636038119076059" style="display:none">"Exactly fifty women were sent into France as secret agents by the Special Operations Executive during the Second World War. Of those, thirty-six survived the war. The other fourteen gave their lives. This book is dedicated to all of them."<br /><br />So. Damn. Good. <br /><br />Ken Follett is best known for his sweeping epics Pillars of the Earth, World Without End, and Fall of Giants which span decades, but in Jackdaws he manages to apply his same talent for engrossing description into a story that takes 10 days. The novel is centered around Flick (aka Felicity) who leads a group of all female secret agents into occupied France to disable an all too important telephone exchange. And if that wasn't difficult enough - the Nazis know she's coming. <br /><br />It's emotional, heart-pounding, and incredibly descriptive. You'll swear you were there and you won't be able to put it down. <br /><br />Oh, yeah. And chicks rule. <br /><br />From the official history:<br />"Women did not normally organize sabotage; but Pearl Witherington, a trained British courier, took over and ran an active Maquis of some two thousand men in Berry with gallantry and distinction after the Gestapo arrested her organizer. She was strongly recommended for an MC (Military Cross), for which women were held ineligible; and received instead a civil MBE, which she returned, observing she had done nothing civil."</span>

<div id="review_382628784" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382628784" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1504452-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220820403p2/1504452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382628784?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1504452-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who claims they like spy novels but secretly loves harlequin romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1504452-becky?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382628784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11993811045957949553">Either KF is a dirty old man or he's taken the adage "sex sells" to heart. For a spy novel, there was an awful lot of flirting and crushes and sex — each instance intended to be more shocking than the last. Rather, each was more ridiculous than the last, resulting in sighs and eye rolling. Lots of eye rolling.<br/><br/>When the author wasn't writing amateur porn and got around to writing the spy part of his spy novel, things didn't pick up as much as you'd think. The plot never gets any serious momentum. </span>
  <span id="freeText11993811045957949553" style="display:none">Either KF is a dirty old man or he's taken the adage "sex sells" to heart. For a spy novel, there was an awful lot of flirting and crushes and sex — each instance intended to be more shocking than the last. Rather, each was more ridiculous than the last, resulting in sighs and eye rolling. Lots of eye rolling.<br /><br />When the author wasn't writing amateur porn and got around to writing the spy part of his spy novel, things didn't pick up as much as you'd think. The plot never gets any serious momentum. It's best described as a formulaic cliche: bad guys on the trail of the good guys (or girls in this case) with lots of close calls, but everything turns out just pat (a little too pat) in the end. All the right characters live, all the wrong characters get what's coming to them, and all the characters you feel neutral towards die. You know, to pull at the reader's heart strings and give the plot that necessary hint of realism. Bleh.<br /><br />A good novel keeps the reader guessing. It at least keeps the reader interested. This pile of cliche and predictability did neither. Only through misguided persistence could I slog through and finish this, and especially at the end, it was only to get it over with already.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11993811045957949553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236628134?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6314397-jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=action">action</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236628134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5844296253229990749">First off, I feel this is a 3.5 but I'm giving it 4, as some of the reviewers on here have been too harsh. <br/><br/>JACKDAWS takes the standard D-Day spy stories but twists it by focusing on the Historical female agents, or, as they were known, something of the unsung heroes. <br/><br/>This particular tale focuses on a female agent who is trying to knock down the phone lines of an SS HQ but needs to do it as cleaning ladies. So, after failing her first attempt, she heads back to the UK where she, and other govt of</span>
  <span id="freeText5844296253229990749" style="display:none">First off, I feel this is a 3.5 but I'm giving it 4, as some of the reviewers on here have been too harsh. <br /><br />JACKDAWS takes the standard D-Day spy stories but twists it by focusing on the Historical female agents, or, as they were known, something of the unsung heroes. <br /><br />This particular tale focuses on a female agent who is trying to knock down the phone lines of an SS HQ but needs to do it as cleaning ladies. So, after failing her first attempt, she heads back to the UK where she, and other govt officials, recruit several female agents for training. <br /><br />All of these women are untrained and have to do a crash course in spycraft. <br /><br />Thereafter, the next half of the book entails the women parachuting into France, some of them getting caught or killed and then moving in on the mission. Expect the usual "B" love story. <br /><br />Story is very good in pacing, and, while some of the characters have the archetypal element, I felt he did a good job creating a diverse selection. <br /><br />When he wrote EYE OF THE NEEDLE the market was less saturated with WWII stories. Now, they're all over the place, so, he has less of the market, the stories overlap more and expectations are higher for newer and newer stories. <br /><br />This one is above average to good but not quite either in definition. If you want to read him for the first time, I'd recommend EYE OF THE NEEDLE.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5844296253229990749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer82195176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8125101546415304456">Jackdaws could have been a very good World War II novel. It's about a group of women operatives (most of them criminals or malcontents) who are given a chance to serve their country and clear their records if they undertake a dangerous mission in France to blow up a Nazi communications center just as the D-Day invasion begins. Yes, the premise is very much a female Dirty Dozen. <br/><br/>The action and characterization of the book are okay but typical. There were just too many sex scenes. And the sad thin</span>
  <span id="freeText8125101546415304456" style="display:none">Jackdaws could have been a very good World War II novel. It's about a group of women operatives (most of them criminals or malcontents) who are given a chance to serve their country and clear their records if they undertake a dangerous mission in France to blow up a Nazi communications center just as the D-Day invasion begins. Yes, the premise is very much a female Dirty Dozen. <br /><br />The action and characterization of the book are okay but typical. There were just too many sex scenes. And the sad thing is those scenes were entirely unecessary. Follett has caved to the contemporary temptation of explicit sex. Too bad. Otherwise, it would have been better.</span>

<div id="review_171078707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171078707" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3047454-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410971765p2/3047454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171078707?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/3047454-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451207524" href="/book/show/5066.Jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3047454-leslie?shelf=popcorn-reading">popcorn-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171078707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5075944421157013812">I picked this up on holiday because I'd read through the books I'd brought and this was the only one among the English-language secondhand paperbacks at the hotel I thought I could stand. It's okay, for what it is. Follett keeps the adrenaline going, but there's not much else here. The main characters are all impossibly good-looking and/or bursting with raw sexual energy (one can practically cast it with the appropriate Hollywood A-listers as one reads). The plot is full of twists, as one would </span>
  <span id="freeText5075944421157013812" style="display:none">I picked this up on holiday because I'd read through the books I'd brought and this was the only one among the English-language secondhand paperbacks at the hotel I thought I could stand. It's okay, for what it is. Follett keeps the adrenaline going, but there's not much else here. The main characters are all impossibly good-looking and/or bursting with raw sexual energy (one can practically cast it with the appropriate Hollywood A-listers as one reads). The plot is full of twists, as one would expect, but the decision to connect it with the D-Day invasion limits the potential for suspense; I mean, we know the invasion happened and it worked, and if the destruction of this telephone exchange plays a role in it then it has to succeed, too, right? The only real question is exactly who will die along the way, and I didn't care about or believe in any of the characters enough to get too anxious about their survival, and most of the deaths were pretty predictable. The book is full of clunky writing. This is just one bad sentence in a book full of bad sentences: "Beautiful women were like the gorgeous French impressionist paintings he collected: having one did not stop you wanting another." Ugh. A stupid cliche, overloaded with adjectives, and quite typical of the book overall. If all you require is adrenalin and you don't care about character or writing or, well, anything else, it's adequate junk reading. Graham Greene and John Le Carre do spy thrillers far, far better, of course, but I'd have been pretty surprised to find a book by either of them in the stack in my Mexican hotel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5075944421157013812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3498406422" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3498406422" />
    <a title="Lobstergirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1910836-lobstergirl"><img alt="Lobstergirl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380256801p2/1910836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3498406422?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lobstergirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lobstergirl" href="/user/show/1910836-lobstergirl">Lobstergirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451207524" href="/book/show/5066.Jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1910836-lobstergirl?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1910836-lobstergirl?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1910836-lobstergirl?shelf=little-free-library">little-free-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3498406422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1190654457357299774"><br/>After a chunk of the French resistance in Reims is killed, a ragtag band of (mostly) English female saboteurs are recruited and trained to take their places and blow up an important telephone exchange operated by the Nazis. (They must be female because they're going in undercover as cleaners.)<br/><br/>Follett is from the Captain Obvious school of writing. In my favorite example, the protagonist Flick and her gay brother Mark go to a gay club in London.<br/><br/><blockquote>A waiter said, "Hello, Markie," and put a hand on Mar</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1190654457357299774" style="display:none"><br />After a chunk of the French resistance in Reims is killed, a ragtag band of (mostly) English female saboteurs are recruited and trained to take their places and blow up an important telephone exchange operated by the Nazis. (They must be female because they're going in undercover as cleaners.)<br /><br />Follett is from the Captain Obvious school of writing. In my favorite example, the protagonist Flick and her gay brother Mark go to a gay club in London.<br /><br /><blockquote>A waiter said, "Hello, Markie," and put a hand on Mark's shoulder, but gave Flick a hostile glare.<br /><br />"Robbie, meet my sister," Mark said. "Her name's Felicity, but we've always called her Flick."<br /><br />The waiter's attitude changed, and he gave Flick a friendly smile. "Very nice to meet you." He showed them a table.<br /><br />Flick guessed that Robbie had suspected she might be a girlfriend, and had resented her for persuading Mark to change sides, as it were. Then he had warmed to her when he learned she was Mark's sister.</blockquote><br /><br />But the novel is not all such tender scenes as this. In fact there is lots and lots of torture. "Some men enjoyed torturing prisoners," Follett writes. "They smiled when their victims screamed, they got erections as they inflicted wounds, and they experienced orgasms during their victims' death throes." After about the sixth explicit Nazi torture scene, some of it extremely disturbingly sexual, readers can be excused for thinking that some men enjoy <i>writing</i> about torture in the same way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1190654457357299774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6314397-jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=ww2-thriller">ww2-thriller</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539531783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15161427078301392592"><b>Another stellar entry into the mind and brilliance of Ken Follett! </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388296072l/5062.jpg' width='250' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><br/><br/>Follet brings us back into the chaos and madness of WW2, and again brilliantly narrates a story that is filled with action, with engaging characters, and most incredibly based on real events! A group of British amateur 'spies' are recruited to lead a suicide mission into occupied France, and infiltrate and explode a key communication relay center north of Paris. Their mission is a-la 'Mission Impossible' scenario. 5 women are ch</span>
  <span id="freeText15161427078301392592" style="display:none"><b>Another stellar entry into the mind and brilliance of Ken Follett! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1388296072l/5062.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><br>Follet brings us back into the chaos and madness of WW2, and again brilliantly narrates a story that is filled with action, with engaging characters, and most incredibly based on real events! A group of British amateur 'spies' are recruited to lead a suicide mission into occupied France, and infiltrate and explode a key communication relay center north of Paris. Their mission is a-la 'Mission Impossible' scenario. 5 women are chosen and led by an experienced resistance fighter 'Flick', and she leads a group of least expected women into a formidable mission! Flick herself is badass, beautiful, and willing to give up anything to flag and country. The other women in the other hand...<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1545890573i/26815156._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><i>Follet again set up a narrative that is filled with action and hyperbole, leading to a crescendo worthy of any hollywood movie! </i>The brilliance in Follett is his ability to express his thoughts elegantly in the most simple way possible! It's a near an impossible trait in a writer, but Follet has masterminded this skillset. His characters are riveting, and there's plenty of violence, some sex and lots of humor in the story. He weaves his characters like chess pieces, and in the end he checkmates without difficulty!<br><br><b> 5 Stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15161427078301392592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2522261604" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2522261604" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2522261604?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451207524" href="/book/show/5066.Jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller-spy">thriller-spy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=world-war-ii">world-war-ii</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2522261604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3135124653853603488">Whenever I read a Ken Follett novel, I expect a lot. Not every book I’ve read by him has been outstanding but most have and so I always hope for one of those. This one certainly qualifies.<br/><br/>It’s a story that takes place during the ten days just prior to the D-Day landings in 1944 during WWII. The French resistance is in full gear, expecting the imminent invasion, even if they don’t know the exact date. The SOE (Special Operations Executive) in London has determined to support the French resistance</span>
  <span id="freeText3135124653853603488" style="display:none">Whenever I read a Ken Follett novel, I expect a lot. Not every book I’ve read by him has been outstanding but most have and so I always hope for one of those. This one certainly qualifies.<br /><br />It’s a story that takes place during the ten days just prior to the D-Day landings in 1944 during WWII. The French resistance is in full gear, expecting the imminent invasion, even if they don’t know the exact date. The SOE (Special Operations Executive) in London has determined to support the French resistance in its efforts to sabotage a key target which, in turn, will greatly aid the success of the invasion. The Gestapo HQ in Paris in the square at Sainte-Cécile, also houses the critical telephonic communications hub. If that were to be taken out of commission, then critical communications to those defending against the invasion forces would be severely impacted.<br /><br />We follow along with Felicity “Flick” Clairet as she builds a team to infiltrate and destroy the communications hub. She chooses all women (Code name: "Jackdaws") so that they can pose as a cleaning crew and make it easier to withstand close scrutiny. Recruitment proves difficult and she must settle for inexperienced women with very little time to train. Most of them are misfits in one fashion or another – comparisons to the Dirty Dozen are not inaccurate.<br /><br />One mark of an excellent thriller story is the quality of the primary antagonist and here, the character of Major Dieter Franck, working on Field Marshal Rommel’s staff, is a wonderfully drawn bad guy. He is extremely dedicated to his task of finding Flick and stopping her mission, and while he can be deliciously evil in his effective torture techniques, he also demonstrates admirable traits of intelligence and dogged determination. <br /><br />The pacing here is perfect. A nice buildup of intrigue and emotion and stressful intensity interspersed with danger as well as softly romantic moments. The pages keep turning despite whatever else might be going on in your life that would drag you away from reading further. The danger is real, and not all characters survive but the ending is deeply satisfying.<br /><br />Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3135124653853603488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732169-sarah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31676120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9538619899629110572">I wasn't sure what to expect from this book. Typically, war based stories are so full of minute details that they detract from the story for me. The plot sounded intriguing though, so I decided to give it a shot. It ended up being one of the better WWII stories that I have read. There was enough background information for me to underdstand the historical reference of the story, but it was balanced by a well developed plot. I like reading stories from a non-American perspective since it is a view</span>
  <span id="freeText9538619899629110572" style="display:none">I wasn't sure what to expect from this book. Typically, war based stories are so full of minute details that they detract from the story for me. The plot sounded intriguing though, so I decided to give it a shot. It ended up being one of the better WWII stories that I have read. There was enough background information for me to underdstand the historical reference of the story, but it was balanced by a well developed plot. I like reading stories from a non-American perspective since it is a viewpoint that I am not normally exposed to. I do not recall learning in school anything about other countries efforts against the Nazi regime during WWII. While this is a fictional story, I think it serves as an interesting view into the role of the French resistance during the war. My only gripe is that the ending seemed a bit contrite. It was rather convenient that her husband that she no longer wished to be with but had too much respect to leave dies, leaving her able to the marry the man she falls in love with.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9538619899629110572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_44050452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44050452" />
    <a title="Bettie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1108123-bettie"><img alt="Bettie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602504374p2/1108123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44050452?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bettie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bettie" href="/user/show/1108123-bettie">Bettie</a>
      </span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44050452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5885463018144020912"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380231169ra/681275.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Read by Kate Reading. Unabridged, on 9 1/2 Tapes<br/><br/>blurb from Publishers Weekly- <i>Time is running out. With D-Day rapidly approaching, the Nazis are actively trying to quash the French resistance. Meanwhile, Britain's Special Operations branch is working hard to supply the resistance with intelligence, supplies and agents. Felicity "Flick" Clairet is one of England's most effective operatives in northern France. Having failed in an assault on the Nazis' main European telephone exchange, she regroups</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5885463018144020912" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380231169ra/681275.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Read by Kate Reading. Unabridged, on 9 1/2 Tapes<br><br>blurb from Publishers Weekly- <i>Time is running out. With D-Day rapidly approaching, the Nazis are actively trying to quash the French resistance. Meanwhile, Britain's Special Operations branch is working hard to supply the resistance with intelligence, supplies and agents. Felicity "Flick" Clairet is one of England's most effective operatives in northern France. Having failed in an assault on the Nazis' main European telephone exchange, she regroups in England for another attempt, this time with an all-female team that will infiltrate the exchange under the guise of a French cleaning staff. Unfortunately, finding female agents fluent in French proves impossible and Flick resorts to crash-training nonprofessionals for the task. Imagine Charlie's Angels (minus the campiness) in The Guns of Navarone. Written in Follett's (Pillars of the Earth, etc.) riveting style and with his penchant for historical detail, the Jackdaws (the codename of the all-girl team) are given a heightened air of authenticity with Kate Reading's performance. She flavors her confident delivery with a wry cynicism that is inherent to Flick's character, and her use of international as well as regional accents keeps the rapid narrative flowing flawlessly.</i><br><br>Shamelessly nicking the tagline: <b>the female dirty dozen</b><br><br>If I was cynical I could say this may be Follett's very own recurring wet dream:<br><br>A dozen females in dress-up<br>S &amp; M<br>Gratuitous sex<br>Nazi goose-steppers<br><br>Sounds like that <a href="http://youtu.be/K08akOt2kuo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>Mel Brookes filmscript</u>
</a> doesn't it. And if not that, maybe it would have been a strong contender for the <a href="http://youtu.be/D9I4nZx8UCs" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>Benny Hill-esque Chase Scene</u>
</a> or toned down this could be an assignment for Charlie's <a href="http://youtu.be/SFaVFFIQk38" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>original trio</u>
</a>.<br><br>All that said, this was rather good, taut and exciting, however it was hard to keep concentrating with all these asides my brain wanted to fling at me.<br><br>ETA - hah! scanning through the reviews here I'm not alone with the brain-swerve into jocularity as there is a reference to <a href="http://youtu.be/7hfHyDSTX50" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <u>'allo 'allo</u>
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5885463018144020912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2580387578" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31265489-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427683864p2/31265489.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2580387578?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/31265489-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13061841-jackdaws">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2580387578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9832112112274937931">This book is dedicated to the 50 unbelievably brave, female secret agents that parachuted into France to gather intelligence or to prepare the invasion on hostile territory during the Second World War. This is one of their (fictional) stories, that is unfortunately all wrong.<br/><br/>First of all, the women: they are basically tough and randy men who just tend to burst into tears, are overly beautiful or just plain stupid. <br/><br/>Second, the plot: we already know the outcome, yes D-Day happened and yes it was a</span>
  <span id="freeText9832112112274937931" style="display:none">This book is dedicated to the 50 unbelievably brave, female secret agents that parachuted into France to gather intelligence or to prepare the invasion on hostile territory during the Second World War. This is one of their (fictional) stories, that is unfortunately all wrong.<br /><br />First of all, the women: they are basically tough and randy men who just tend to burst into tears, are overly beautiful or just plain stupid. <br /><br />Second, the plot: we already know the outcome, yes D-Day happened and yes it was a success, so instead the plot uses blunt torture, random sex quickly leading to love and throws in some homosexuals and queers to make it more diverse. Oh yes and all the Nazis’ decision are always plot-relevant meaning that if the author needed someone to survive he was sure to not be tortured right away but for some strategic reason only put away. Overall, this made everything too predictable. I have to confess that by the last 20% I wanted to know how it all ended, but really, I rather I haven’t read this. It is certainly not worthy of these amazingly brave women!<br /><br />There was one quote that moved me:<br /><br /><i> My dear Papa, I am doing well in school although Dr Richter’s classroom has been bombed. Fortunately it was night time and the school was empty. </i><br /><br />2.5 stars, rounding down.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9832112112274937931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I always enjoy Ken Follet's approach to history--crackerjack pacing, strong dialogue, and a deep desire to entertain. If only all writers cared as much about their audience's enjoyment as Follet </span>
  <span id="freeText13423825243985200796" style="display:none">Ken Follet achieves the nearly impossible task of creating genuine suspense about an event that is well-known, with fresh characters, clever plotting, and surprising twists on an old story. You will enjoy this book on a long plane flight, or just sitting out on your porch during the lazy days of summer. I always enjoy Ken Follet's approach to history--crackerjack pacing, strong dialogue, and a deep desire to entertain. If only all writers cared as much about their audience's enjoyment as Follet does, TV would become obsolete.</span>

<div id="review_177439039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177439039" />
    <a title="J.F. Penn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1696949-j-f-penn"><img alt="J.F. Penn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338284273p2/1696949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177439039?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.F. Penn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.F. Penn" href="/user/show/1696949-j-f-penn">J.F. Penn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1696949-j-f-penn?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177439039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17420492737492384649">Full video review here : <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://mysterythriller.tv/jackdaws-by-ken-follett/'>http://mysterythriller.tv/jackdaws-by...</a><br/><br/>I have always found Ken Follett too verbose but this book was an excellent fast read with a great female lead character. Flick Clairet is one of a select group of women helping the French Resistance during the final years of the Second World War. She is married to a French man, the leader of the resistance in Reims and in the opening sequence we see a group of them fail to overcome a telephone exchange that is crucial to the German</span>
  <span id="freeText17420492737492384649" style="display:none">Full video review here : <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://mysterythriller.tv/jackdaws-by-ken-follett/">http://mysterythriller.tv/jackdaws-by...</a><br /><br />I have always found Ken Follett too verbose but this book was an excellent fast read with a great female lead character. Flick Clairet is one of a select group of women helping the French Resistance during the final years of the Second World War. She is married to a French man, the leader of the resistance in Reims and in the opening sequence we see a group of them fail to overcome a telephone exchange that is crucial to the Germans.   Several of the local resistance members are captured, tortured and a German intelligence officer is able to start unravelling the underground team there. He is a ruthless torturer although we also see his cultured side and his love for a Jewish mistress. He even gets terrible migraines when he has to torture people so Follett manages to create a villain who is still believable and not a caricature of the evil Nazi.<br /><br />After the failure of the team, Flick is determined to get back to the exchange and blow it up, creating a critical gap in communications at the same time as the Allied forces invade. The timing is crucial and the book is basically her mission back to Reims in order to accomplish this task. The only way in is to recruit other women to act as an all-female team disguised as cleaners. In that way they can get into the exchange and blow up the communications. The women Flick recruits have been rejected by other services and are generally unsuitable, a ragtag bunch including a convicted murderer, a Cockney explosives expert thief, a lesbian aristocrat and a transvestite whose lover had been killed by the Germans. The journey the women take, the danger they get into is the crux of the story. No spoilers but as in real life, they don’t all make it.<br /><br />Flick is characterized as a hard soldier in that she is able to shoot a traitor and and fight in hand to hand combat, but she also has a softer side and is able to love and think about marriage. I like these types of characters and she made the story believable. She and Dieter, the Nazi interrogator are by far the strongest characters in the book and it really was a battle between these two throughout the book.<br /><br />Although you know that of course the Allies will win in the end, you still don’t know until the last pages whether the team will survive. I enjoyed the book, reading it on a windy, wild Auckland day in pretty much one sitting. It’s a thriller with an intelligent female heroine. Recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17420492737492384649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_142376948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142376948" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/737152-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591837102p2/737152.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142376948?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/737152-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Irene by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2949949-rebecca-schneider">Rebecca Schneider</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/737152-irene?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142376948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13932166715973314139">The problem I have with historical fiction is that I always figure there must be plenty of amazing true stories from the same time period, so why not read about those? <i>Jackdaws</i> brings attention to the Special Operations Executive, the British military division responsible for secret operatives sent behind enemy lines. According to a note in the book, fifty women really were sent into France as spies during World War II. So what are <i>their</i> stories? I'm sure they're as fascinating, or even more so,</span>
  <span id="freeText13932166715973314139" style="display:none">The problem I have with historical fiction is that I always figure there must be plenty of amazing true stories from the same time period, so why not read about those? <i>Jackdaws</i> brings attention to the Special Operations Executive, the British military division responsible for secret operatives sent behind enemy lines. According to a note in the book, fifty women really were sent into France as spies during World War II. So what are <i>their</i> stories? I'm sure they're as fascinating, or even more so, than anything anyone could make up.<br /><br />Well, putting my own prejudices aside, the book was good. It held my interest enough that I looked forward to reading it each night, but not so much that it kept me up later than I wanted. It's the kind of book that does well as a TV substitute. It reads like a movie, it's entertaining, and it's a bit suspenseful. <br /><br />Just like a movie, though, there was what I would consider superfluous romance that distracted from the action and actual plot. <br /><br />Frequently when a book includes foreign words or references to political or military organizations, I'm annoyed that the reader is assumed to have sufficient knowledge of the references; I appreciate it when additional context is given, or when a foreign phrase is subtly translated. However, I dare say that Ken Follett goes overboard: Is it really necessary to explicitly define the word "suffragette"?<br /><br />Finally, near the end, I think the main character Flick made two uncharacteristic moves - she made a decision against her better judgment, and she didn't react quickly enough given the circumstances. I wonder why Follett weakened her character after spending so much time before and after developing her character. Maybe just to show that she's human and makes mistakes, too.<br /><br />Anyway, I wasn't blown away by the book, but it's easy reading and the kind of book that's good for passing the time. Since Ken Follett is such a prolific writer, I'll probably pick up more of his books from the library from time to time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13932166715973314139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17367715588753485304">A team of six women are sent from England to France just before the Allied invasion of Normandy in June, 1944. Their job is to destroy a German communications system that sends information for the bad guys from France back to Germany. The problem is, it's not that easy.   <span id="freeText17367715588753485304" style="display:none">A team of six women are sent from England to France just before the Allied invasion of Normandy in June, 1944. Their job is to destroy a German communications system that sends information for the bad guys from France back to Germany. The problem is, it's not that easy. They are parachuted on to enemy soil and have to work very, very hard to avoid all the traps laid for them. A terrific character named Flick Claret is opposed by an evil Gestapo torture master by the name of Dieter Franck. You can count on Ken Follett for a rollicking historical fiction saga, but when compared to two of the top ten best books I have EVER read, The Pillars of the Earth and World Without End, this one just doesn't measure up. Can't quite give it four stars.</span>

<div id="review_676675776" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676675776" />
    <a title="Alicja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4745220-alicja"><img alt="Alicja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411681297p2/4745220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/676675776?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicja" href="/user/show/4745220-alicja">Alicja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=minor-lgbt-themes">minor-lgbt-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=war-military-battle">war-military-battle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=early-20th-century">early-20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=world-war-ii">world-war-ii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4745220-alicja?shelf=assasin-spy">assasin-spy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676675776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16122550687429255665">rating: 3/5 <br/><br/>Days before D-Day there is a high priority Nazi target on French soil that needs to be destroyed. However, there is a catch, only an all-female team can gain access to it. Flick is put in charge of this quickly formed, ragtag team as they attempt to fulfill their dangerous mission.<br/><br/>Loved the action, the plot, and the kick-ass female protagonist. The POV mostly alternated between Flick, the British agent on French soil, and Dieter, a Nazi commander. I had chills from viewing through a </span>
  <span id="freeText16122550687429255665" style="display:none">rating: 3/5 <br /><br />Days before D-Day there is a high priority Nazi target on French soil that needs to be destroyed. However, there is a catch, only an all-female team can gain access to it. Flick is put in charge of this quickly formed, ragtag team as they attempt to fulfill their dangerous mission.<br /><br />Loved the action, the plot, and the kick-ass female protagonist. The POV mostly alternated between Flick, the British agent on French soil, and Dieter, a Nazi commander. I had chills from viewing through a window into Dieter's head, especially during the torture scenes which left me feeling uncomfortable; he seemed to be the best developed and most complex character in the entire novel. <br /><br />Most action occurred as Flick commanded a female unit in an attack on a Nazi target while Dieter pursued them. The plot revolved around a topic I've never read about before, British agents working with the French resistance during WWII. The plot was exciting, quick, fun to read, and kept me turning the page.<br /><br />It's a great fast-paced action book; however, the character development mostly just wasn't there. There is a huge supporting cast of secondary characters but they are all two-dimensional (with two characters behaving in such an idiotic way that just didn't seem believable). Some of the characters are LGBT, they are badly written and stereotypical, but the straight characters seemed like they were taken from a stereotype encyclopedia so I didn't take offense. I couldn't connect with any of them. <br /><br />Additionally, the romance element seemed like something lifted from a Harlequin novel. The sex scene was the most awful thing I've ever read and completely unnecessary. And the ending was too neat, wrapping up everything just oh so perfectly.<br /><br />If you are looking for a non-cognitively involving but fast-paced action-y quick read, then this is the novel to pick up. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16122550687429255665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122689508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122689508" />
    <a title="Ed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1090620-ed"><img alt="Ed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208403306p2/1090620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122689508?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ed" href="/user/show/1090620-ed">Ed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Spy story and Follett fans.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1090620-ed?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1090620-ed?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1090620-ed?shelf=spy-political-thriller">spy-political-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122689508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer323750038813909155">This offering of Ken Follett, while not up to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/92364.Eye_of_the_Needle' title='Eye of the Needle by Ken Follett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eye of the Needle</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth' title='The Pillars of the Earth by Ken Follett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Pillars of the Earth</a> was nevertheless a good book to have on a trip with many delays due to weather and mechanical problems.<br/><br/>It chronicles the travails of a group of British women who are tasked to destroy a German telephone exchange just before D-Day, important because it was the main conduit for most of the military phone traffic between France and Berlin .<br/><br/>The plot is well-developed but I find Follett's characterizations to </span>
  <span id="freeText323750038813909155" style="display:none">This offering of Ken Follett, while not up to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/92364.Eye_of_the_Needle" title="Eye of the Needle by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">Eye of the Needle</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5043.The_Pillars_of_the_Earth" title="The Pillars of the Earth by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Pillars of the Earth</a> was nevertheless a good book to have on a trip with many delays due to weather and mechanical problems.<br /><br />It chronicles the travails of a group of British women who are tasked to destroy a German telephone exchange just before D-Day, important because it was the main conduit for most of the military phone traffic between France and Berlin .<br /><br />The plot is well-developed but I find Follett's characterizations to be a little less than believable. I like my heroes to have more warts. My two biggest problems with the story are the incredible number of coincidences that work in the saboteurs' favor and the various love interest sub-plots that add melodrama but very little else to the narrative.<br /><br />While certainly better than some of his later offerings like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5052.Code_to_Zero" title="Code to Zero by Ken Follett" rel="nofollow noopener">Code to Zero</a>, This book did not motivate me to read more of Follett's work than I have already read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="323750038813909155" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1096864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096864" />
    <a title="haley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79349-haley"><img alt="haley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1178623538p2/79349.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096864?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="haley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="haley" href="/user/show/79349-haley">haley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79349-haley?shelf=worldwartwo">worldwartwo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8902508628408387058">Let me preface this by saying that I love historical fiction having anything to do with Europe between the years 1900-1945. World War Two dramas are usually filled with such drama and atmosphere that I can't help but be excited by it. I'm not sure why, but I love it.<br/><br/>This book found me while I was on my French Resistance kick, and it's about a squad of British Female Spies that parachute into occupied France to aid in the Resistance. Sure, it's a mass-market paperback thriller, but it's a fun, fa</span>
  <span id="freeText8902508628408387058" style="display:none">Let me preface this by saying that I love historical fiction having anything to do with Europe between the years 1900-1945. World War Two dramas are usually filled with such drama and atmosphere that I can't help but be excited by it. I'm not sure why, but I love it.<br /><br />This book found me while I was on my French Resistance kick, and it's about a squad of British Female Spies that parachute into occupied France to aid in the Resistance. Sure, it's a mass-market paperback thriller, but it's a fun, fast-paced read and I love the authenticity of detail, from the description of the spy mindset while being followed, to the images of "ersatz coffee" that was used while regular coffee was being rationed. Ersatz coffee, by the way, was usually ground and roasted chicory. Not terribly tasty. <br /><br />What intrigues me most about this book is what shocked me about the movie Charlotte Gray. Women are usually depicted as nurses and faithful homebodies during WWII. The fact that many women risked their lives and actually parachuted into France blows my mind. Most male soldiers didn't even parachute, let alone into occupied enemy territory. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8902508628408387058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
